## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from exponential to logistic to more complex density-dependent and time-dependent growth models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic minus catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Time-dependent logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t) (logistic with time-varying growth rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with proportional removal)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonally varying growth)
- Delayed density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (growth with time-proxy for delayed effects)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density-dependent growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt proportional to P) → exponential-type growth indicating density-independent per-capita rate
- Quadratic term in P (P² appears) → density-dependent feedback such as logistic competition or cooperative effects
- Logarithmic dependence on P (log(P) appears) → Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative rather than additive density effects
- Fractional power of P (P^c with 0<c<1) → sub-linear growth typical of surface-area-limited or metabolic scaling processes
- Product of two linear factors in P → Allee effect or bistability with two equilibrium points
- Ratio P/(1+cP) structure → contest competition or resource saturation in per-capita terms
- Explicit time dependence with multiplicative P → non-autonomous growth with changing environmental conditions
- Trigonometric function of time multiplied by growth term → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on population
- Difference of two power laws in P → competing growth and mortality processes with different scaling exponents (von Bertalanffy type)
- Negative coefficient on highest power of P → bounded population with stable carrying capacity equilibrium

## GT Analysis

Let me simplify the GT numerical expression:
```
0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.0971*P))*P
```

Let me expand each term:

**Term 1:** `0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P`
= `0.17*(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)*P`

Let me expand `(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)`:
= `P/1.047 − P²/(1.047×10.21) − 1 + P/10.21`
= `−P²/10.69 + P/1.047 + P/10.21 − 1`
= `−P²/10.69 + P(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − 1`

Multiply by 0.17*P:
= `−0.17*P³/10.69 + 0.17*P²(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − 0.17*P`

**Term 2:** `0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P`
= `0.17*P − 0.17*P²/10.21`

**Term 3:** `0.17*(1 − exp(−0.0971*P))*P`
= `0.17*P − 0.17*P*exp(−0.0971*P)`

**Combining all terms:**
- P³ coefficient: `−0.17/10.69 ≈ −0.0159`
- P² coefficient: `0.17*(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − 0.17/10.21 = 0.17/1.047 ≈ 0.1624`
- P coefficient: `−0.17 + 0.17 + 0.17 = 0.17`
- Exponential term: `−0.17*P*exp(−0.0971*P)`

So GT ≈ **c₀P³ + c₁P² + c₂P + c₃·P·exp(c₄·P)** where c₄ < 0.

This is: `aP³ + bP² + cP + d·P·exp(e·P)`

Now let me check candidates for this structure:

**Candidate 41:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + c3 + c4*exp(Pc5)`
= aP³ + bP² + cP + d + e·exp(fP). This has a constant term and exp(fP), not P·exp(fP). **No match.**

**Candidate 40:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + c4 + c5*exp(Pc6)`
= aP³ + bP² + (c2+c3)P + c4 + c5·exp(c6·P). Same issue. **No match.**

**Candidate 10:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + c3*exp(Pc4) + c5 + c6*exp(Pc7)`
Two exponentials plus polynomial. Could one exponential approximate P·exp(eP)? No, P·exp(eP) is not exp(fP). **No match.**

**Candidate 7:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + P^c3·c4 + c5 + c6·exp(Pc7)`
If c3=1, P^c3·c4 = c4·P, combining with Pc2. But we need P·exp(eP), which isn't available. However, setting c3=1 gives polynomial + exp. **No match.**

**Candidate 35:** `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + Pc3/(Pc1+c2) + Pc4/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5·exp(Pc6)/(Pc1+c2) + c7/(Pc1+c2) + c8·exp(Pc6)/(Pc1+c2) + c9/(Pc1+c2)`

If c1=0, c2=1: `P²c0 + P(c3+c4) + c5·P·exp(c6·P) + (c7+c9) + c8·exp(c6·P)`

This gives: aP² + bP + c·P·exp(dP) + e + f·exp(dP). We need aP³ + bP² + cP + d·P·exp(eP). Missing P³ term, and has unwanted constant and exp terms. Setting c8=0 and (c7+c9)=0: aP² + bP + c·P·exp(dP). Still missing P³. **No match.**

After careful analysis, the GT has the form `aP³ + bP² + cP + d·P·exp(eP)`, and none of the candidates can produce this exact functional form.

[NO MATCH]

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this. Let me use α = 0.17, a = 1.047, b = 10.21, β = 0.097.

**Term 1:** α*(−1 + P/a)*(1 − P/b)*P
= α*(P/a − 1)*(1 − P/b)*P
= α*P*(P/a − 1)(1 − P/b)
= α*P*[P/a − P²/(ab) − 1 + P/b]
= α*[P²/a − P³/(ab) − P + P²/b]

**Term 2:** α*(1 − P/b)*P = α*[P − P²/b]

**Term 3:** α*(1 − exp(−β*P))*P = α*[P − P*exp(−β*P)]

Combining Terms 1+2+3:
= α*[P²/a − P³/(ab) − P + P²/b + P − P²/b + P − P*exp(−β*P)]
= α*[P²/a − P³/(ab) + P − P*exp(−β*P)]

So GT = α*P²/a − α*P³/(ab) + α*P − α*P*exp(−β*P)

Numerically:
- Coefficient of P³: −0.17/(1.047×10.21) ≈ −0.0159
- Coefficient of P²: 0.17/1.047 ≈ 0.1623
- Coefficient of P: 0.17
- Exponential term: −0.17*P*exp(−0.097*P)

So **GT = c_3*P³ + c_2*P² + c_1*P + c_exp*P*exp(−β*P)**

The basis functions are: **P³, P², P, P·exp(−βP)** where β > 0.

This is crucial: the GT contains a term **P·exp(−βP)** (with negative exponent coefficient since β > 0).

Now let me check each candidate for structural compatibility.

### Candidates with `t` dependence (can set t-coefficients to 0):
Candidates 24, 25, 27, 28, 30, 31, 36, 38, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46, 47 contain `t`. I can set t-related coefficients to 0 only if the t-terms can be independently zeroed.

### Key question for each candidate:
Does it have the basis functions {P³, P², P, P·exp(cP)} where c can be negative?

**Candidate 35:** P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + Pc3/(Pc1+c2) + Pc4/(Pc1+c2) + P·c5·exp(Pc6)/(Pc1+c2) + c7/(Pc1+c2) + c8·exp(Pc6)/(Pc1+c2) + c9/(Pc1+c2)

**Candidate 39:** P³c0 + P²c1 + P^c2·c3 + c4·exp(Pc5) + c6
